# 6 Types of Negative Emotions

# 6.1 Introduction

This chapter reports on the types of negative emotions that clients display when they disclose the ganqing violation-induced discordant rapport (hereafter GQVI discordant rapport) that exists between them and NPTPs during psychotherapy sessions. In 6.2, I outline the types of negative emotions triggered by clients' unmet ganqing expectations. In 6.3, I present the types of negative emotions evoked by clients' unfulfilled ganqing obligations. The unmet expectations and unfulfilled obligations point to two different types of discordant rapport between clients and the NPTPs. Accordingly, the interlink between the types of discordant rapport and the types of negative emotions is discussed.

# 6.2 Anger/anger and Sadness

People's perceptions of disharmonious relations or discordant rapport result in negative emotions. When people find their behavioural expectations are not met, they would react with (1) anger or (2) anger and sadness. The following examples focus on clients' self-reports of the unmet ganqing expectations and their negative emotional reactions.

# 6.2.1 Lack of Feelings as Rapport Threat

Ganqing involves empathy and understanding people's feelings (Chen & Chen 2004; Yen et al. 2017; Chang 2018). This means when the Chinese communicate with the guanxi members (i.e., NPTPs in this study) with whom they are close or have a long-term relationship, the Chinese expect to be treated by the NPTPs with empathic feelings. If this ganqing expectation is not met, it would pose threats to the rapport between the two parties and result in GQVI discordant rapport, which would trigger clients' anger at the NPTPs.

For the following and the other extracts presented in Chapter 6, the turns marked with  $(\longrightarrow)$  indicate the interactional sequences in which clients' negative emotions occur, while the utterances underlined show how the discordant rapport is characterized as GQVI discordant rapport (i.e., it is caused by unmet ganqing expectations or unfulfilled ganqing obligations). C stands for the client and T refers to the therapist.

Extract 6.1 C's negative emotions occur when she discloses the prior interaction with her close friends.

1 C：我跟高中最好的那个朋友，我就唯一这么几个朋友，有一次就坐在车里，他们就说不明白我为什么把对别人的恶意转嫁给自己，说我傻，就把自己给气病了……不明白我的自卑是哪儿来的，说我不负责任，脆弱，不坚强，自己不让自己长大，就说自己不努力。

I was sitting in the car with my best friends from high school, I only had such a few friends. While we were just sitting in the car one time, they said that they couldn't understand why I turned other people's ill-will towards myself. They were calling me stupid since I pissed myself off ... They couldn't understand where my low self-esteem came from, saying I was irresponsible, fragile, not strong enough, and not letting myself grow up, and just saying that I didn't make an effort.

2 T: 嗯。Mm.

3 C: 就是他们最后把我怼哭了，我说不过他们了，几个人七嘴八舌的，就那么-本来就表达得很快。我就想说的话就说不出来，就憋得慌，好难受，最后没办法，就只能哭。他们说我不负责任，然后没想过父母，然后得这种病，也<我觉得特别不公平，他们这么说，也不是我自己愿意得的>。

They finally made me cry, it was difficult for me to argue back. They were such fast speakers that  $\mathrm{o}$  I was just denied to say what I wanted to say, I was holding back and was uncomfortable, and finally, I had no choice but to cry  $\mathrm{o}$ . They said I was irresponsible, because I didn't think about my parents, and I got this disease, which was also  $-<\mathrm{o}$  I thought it was extremely unfair that they were saying this. Being sick was not something I had wanted  ${>}^{\circ}$ .

4 T：你怎么看待他们所说的这个？

What do you think about what they were saying?

5 C: 没有人能感同身受。

So no one can really feel the same feelings as you do.

6 T: 可能我们的第一反应是你站着说话不腰疼。

Maybe our first reaction is if you don't put yourself into my shoes, you wouldn't know what I meant.

7 C: 反正不愿意接受这种说法。

Anyway, I am not willing to accept that.

8 T：或者当我们听到这种说法的时候会觉得特别孤独，

Or we'll feel particularly lonely when we hear it,

9 C: 嗯。

Mm.

10 T：会觉得他们，指望他们理解是不可能了。

It's impossible to expect them to understand.

11

C: 就是因为从大学的时候就觉得，就说不能指望另一个人理解你，所以说有的事情就不要-不要和别人说……

Just because I have felt that I couldn't expect another person to understand me from college, so certain things cannot be shared with anyone…

C discloses how she is negatively commented on by her close friends. Rather than expressing anger through sonorant cues (e.g., the high pitch register or fast tempo), C's anger towards them is displayed with more subdued cues here (Selting 2010: 239): in a low voice and slow tempo. From the negative assessment ('I thought it was extremely unfair, they were saying this', Turn 3), her anger towards them is explicitly demonstrated (Räabis et al. 2019). From C's complaints against her friends, the discordant rapport between the two parties is observable. Locating C's anger within the interactional sequences in which it occurs, a link between C's emotional reactions and the discordant rapport can be made (Spencer-Oatey 2005; Culpeper 2011).

The nature of the discordant rapport (i.e., ganqing violation-induced) is reflected in interlocutors' meta-pragmatic comments made in the subsequent turns. When C is invited by T to mention her friends' behaviour, C states that 'no one can share the same feelings with you' (Turn 5). When T responds in the next turn (Turn 6), he takes some part of the interpretation from C's prior turn and formulates it (Vehvilainen 2008: 130), in this way to show his acceptance and acknowledgement of C's argument. Moreover, T comments on C's friends as not standing in C's shoes (Turn 6) and not understanding C's feelings (Turn 10). By making these comments, T and C evoke evaluations of a threat to ganqing. This unmet ganqing expectation threatened the rapport between the two parties and evoked C's anger. The next example further illustrates how a client's anger emerges from her perceptions of GQVI discordant rapport, the latter of which is threatened by her mother's de-empathic behaviour.

Extract 6.2 C and her parents run a curtain in shop and C's mother is so devoted to the business that she neglects to care for her daughter.

1 C: 我真的挺不了，我确实是太累了。包括我怀孕的时候，整个人状态确实不行，确实太累了。我妈妈就说，“↑怎么着↑怎么就坚持不了，我们那个年代我们年轻的时候哪有这个条件，我们都能坚持，↑>你怎么就不行啊？你怎么就不能咬咬牙坚持坚持<？”我怀孕我没休息一天，我一直到最后阵痛了，把所有事情处理完了再去医院。

I really couldn't insist anymore. I was too tired. Even when I was pregnant, I was not in good condition, and I was too tired. My mother complained to me, '↑ > Why do you not insist on it now<? You should try your best to insist on and continue working'. I kept working when I was pregnant, I didn't stop working until the birth pangs came, and I finished all the work before I went to the hospital.

T: 那不知道的还以为不是亲妈呢, 是吧? 有没有怀疑过是不是亲妈?

Those who don't know about your family might think she is not your own mother? right? Have you ever suspected that she is not your own mother?

3 C：那没有，怀疑倒没有。怀孕最后一个月，孩子正是长的时候嘛，我最

后那一个月几乎没怎么吃午饭，忙到吃不了，吃不上。好不容易我卖完了，一回头，老太太又揽了一个人，>一份儿接一份儿的，一份接一份儿的<。

No, no doubt about that. During the last month of my pregnancy, and that time it was high time for the baby's growth. I didn't have lunch nearly for the whole month, I was too busy. Finally, I finished the work at hand, and when I looked behind me, my mom solicited another customer,  $>$  one by one, one by one<.

4 T：她-她感觉像个教练一样哦，在训练一个拳击手。

She - she felt like a coach who was training a boxer.

5 C: 嗯，我都饿得不行了。我说“妈呀，我实在不行了”。我这么多年，有时不吃饭太正常的事儿了，吃不上饭。怀孕的时候挺不了，说“妈呀，我太饿了，你帮我买点啥，我吃一口”。我妈买了点儿带饼的咸菜，说“↑>你吃吧！<”我一下子就真的很想哭。你说你女儿马上半个月要生了，这么累，每天挣这么多钱，真的很累得慌……Well, I'm starving. I said, 'OMG, I just can't'. I've been doing this for years, and it's not unusual for me not to be able to eat sometimes. When I was pregnant, I couldn't stand it, so I said, 'Mum, I'm so hungry, buy me something, I'll have a bite'. My mother bought some pickles with cakes and said, ‘↑>Eat it! <’ I really wanted to cry. Her daughter is about to give birth in half a month, and she is so tired, earning so much money every day, it's really tiring…

6 T: ¥她确实挺有病, 是吧? ¥确实挺变态的, 是吧?

¥ She's sick, isn't she? ¥ She must be psychologically perverted, is she psycho?

C：那倒也不是，她觉得自己挺正常的。

That's not true. She feels she is normal.

8 T：问题是她不觉得这是个问题，这不就是很变态吗？

The problem is that she doesn't think it's a problem, isn't she psychologically perverted?

9 C:￥啊,对,对

￥Ah, yes, yes.

T: 别说亲妈了，是吧？就是老板都-都不能这么对员工。

Let alone your mother, right? Even the boss cannot treat their employees in such a way.

When C discloses social interactions between her and her mother, anger, a typical type of other-condemning emotion (Haidt 2003), is displayed through the following emotional cues: (1) phonetic-prosodic cues. When C discloses how she is inattentively treated, she speaks in a high-pitch register ( $^\circ \uparrow >$  Why do you not insist on it now<, Turn 1), extra-high pitch peaks, tempo changes, and dense attenuations (Turn 5). These cues, as noted in Selting (2010: 243), are explicit indicators of C's anger. (2) Verbal cues that are reflected in the intensifiers (Räabis et al. 2019), for instance, intensifying via repetition ('one by one, one by one <', Turn 3) and the adverb ('too tired', Turn 1). (3) 'Quotes' or 'recreations of others' speech' (Besnier

1990: 426) ('My mother complained to me', Turn 1; '↑>Eat it! <', Turn 5). By upgrading and aggravating C's negative emotional stance (anger) through these linguistic and non-linguistic means (Cekaite 2016: 137), C's strong anger at her mother is communicated.

By locating C's anger in the interactional sequence in which it occurs, it can be found that it responds to the disharmony that exists between C and her mother (Işik-Güler & Ruhi 2010). In Turn 1, Turn 3 and Turn 5, C complains about how her mother does not demonstrate an understanding of her situation and does not respond to her feelings, wants, and needs (Fukushima 2015; Chang 2018). In doing so, C projects a 'negative assessment' of her mother's person, evoking evaluations of a threat to ganqing. Upon hearing C's self-disclosure, T meta/comments the mother's behaviour by using rude and aggressive words ('be sick', 'psychologically perverted', Turn 6). In Turn 10, T initiates another moral evaluation to criticize the mother's behaviour. These meta-pragmatic comments reveal that the mother's ignorance of ganqing has caused disharmony between her and her daughter, and has evoked C's anger towards her mother.

To treat specific guanxi members with ganqing not only means understanding the others' feelings (cf. Extract 6-1), understanding their situation, and responding to their needs (cf. Extract 6-2) but also means refraining from saying or doing something that would hurt the other's feelings (Fukushima & Haugh 2014: 167). Otherwise, it would pose a threat to the rapport between the two parties and evoke one party's negative emotions.

Extract 6.3 C, a middle-aged man, complains about his wife for her hurtful utterances.

<table><tr><td>1</td><td>C: 她现在几乎于那种吹毛求疵的状态。如果你早晨煮俩鸡蛋，剥了。 She is now almost in a state of fault-finding. If I boil two eggs in the morning and peel them.</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>T: 嗯, Mm,</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>C: 因为有时候鸡蛋剥不好之后，不好看。 Because sometimes when the eggs are not peeled properly, they don&#x27;t look very good.</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>T: 嗯, Mm,</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>→ C: 她很愤怒，“↑啊，像狗啃似的，剥的什么呀！↑啥都干不好。”一顿说，就这种苛刻状态。其实谁希望呢？谁都知道那个鸡蛋不好剥，所以要慢慢一点点剥。她有时候也剥坏啊，那你说-她就是挑剔你((咂嘴))。 你要是想回家想躺一会儿，他就该说你了，“↑啊，你又这么懒，躺那会儿。” The peeled egg made her angry. ‘↑It&#x27;s like a dog&#x27;s gnawing. What are you peeling! You can&#x27;t do anything well’. A criticism following up, a harsh state as such. No one wants it - everyone knows that it is difficult to peel the egg, and you need to do it very slowly. She cannot do it well sometimes. She is picky about you ((smacking the lips)). If you want to go home and lie down for a while, she blames you, ‘↑Ah, you are so lazy again, lie down there’.</td></tr></table>

6 T: 所以好像-好多年都没有得到过真正的安宁。

So, it seems - we haven't had any real peace for years.

7 C: 有时候真是((长声叹气)), 其实男人有时候压力挺大的,

你知道的但是在她面前，她总觉得你这个男人应该>

怎么怎么怎么的<((长声叹气))整天说教，整天给你-管你，

Sometimes it is true ((a long sigh)). You know, men sometimes have a lot of pressure. But in front of her, she thinks you're a man who's supposed to be  $>$  et cetera et cetera  $<$  ((a long sigh)) She is preaching all the time, lecturing you about all the time-whatever,

8 T: 嗯,

Mm,

9 C：你做得挺好的时候，她从来不会说你这事儿挺好。有一点点

瑕疵或者怎么怎么的，她会毫不留情地，把你骂得狗血-喷头，>那种挖苦，或者那种那种那种那种< =

When you're good at something, she never says it's good. If there is a slight blemish or whatever, she'll mercilessly lash out at you,  $>$  that sarcasm, or that kind of that kind of that kind of  $<=$

10 T: =极其伤人的

$=$  Extremely hurtful

11 C: =极其伤人……

$=$  Extremely hurtful…

The disharmonious relationship between C and his wife is observable, as indicated by his complaints and criticisms towards her. When complaining, a strong degree of anger is displayed through the following cues: (1) prosodic means. When C 'quotes' or recreates his wife's speech (Besnier 1990: 426), he speaks with a high pitch register (Reber 2008, 2012) (' $\uparrow$  It's like a dog's gnawing. What are you peeling!', Turn 5). He also complains in a fast tempo (' $\rightarrow$ that sarcasm $\cdots$ $\prec$ ', Turn 9). (2) Rhetorical means. For instance, by repeating in a full, partial, or modified way, and the repetition of words and syntactic structures (Räabis et al. 2019) ('preaching all the time, lecturing you about all the time', Turn 7). (3) Lexical-semantic means. For instance, C comments on his wife's behaviour by using lexical items with negative connotations (ibid: 2) ('a harsh state', Turn 5; 'mercilessly', Turn 9). By producing a markedly loud sound, and effectively upgrading his negative stance towards his wife (Cekaite 2016: 147), C displays strong anger towards his wife.

C's anger is caused by the GQVI discordant rapport that exists between him and his wife. Specifically, C's complaining way of speaking focuses on how his wife shows little consideration for his feelings and criticizes him 'merceilessly' (Turn 3, Turn 5, Turn 7). This complaint projects a relational separation from his wife and indicates the disharmony between them (Spencer-Oatey & Xing 2003; Arundale 2010). Furthermore, T meta/comments the wife's behaviour as 'extremely hurtful' (Turn 10). By delivering such a 'moral evaluation' (Kádár & Haugh 2013) and projecting a negative evaluation of the wife's person, T displays evaluations of a threat to ganqing. C's echoing in the next turn shows his acceptance of

C's evaluation (Ferrara 1994; Pawelczyk 2011: 124). In summary, from C's complaints towards his wife and the moral evaluations of the wife's person, it can be drawn that the wife's violation of ganqing has caused disharmony between the two parties, leading to C's anger.

# 6.2.2 Anger and Sadness: Lack of Feelings as Rapport Threat

In some cases, when the interlocutors perceive there exists GQVI discordant rapport between them and the guanxi members, with the guanxi members' lack of feelings as rapport threats, the interlocutors would not only react with anger but also with sadness.

Extract 6.4 C reports on her prior interaction with her parents. C has experienced difficulties in her job and is expected to be understood and supported by her parents, but the real situation runs contrary to her expectations.

1 T：如果父母成为我们主心骨的话，我们也不会在外面这么难的啊。很少和他们联系吗？

...If our parents become our backbone, life wouldn't have been so difficult for us, do you rarely contact them?

2 C：他俩之前感情也不好，

They didn't have a good relationship before,

3 T：嗯。

Mm.

4 C：没法儿说，比如你加班的意思，就是“你-↑>不要再这样干了啊<”，你能说什么啊？你抱怨一下，他们就说你不要在这儿干了；

或者你抱怨一下，他们就说“↑>你不是有自尊吗？

你为什么还和那个人在一起啊？<”

It is difficult to say, for example, if you work overtime, they will say  $-\uparrow >$  You won't do it again<. What else could you say? If you complain, then they will tell you not to work here anymore; or if you complain, they will say,  $\uparrow >$  Don't you have self-esteem? Why are you still with that guy?

5 T: 什么也说不了。

Nothing we could complain to our parents.

6 C: %怎么抱怨啊%

% How to complain%

T: 给不了我们要的那种支持。

They can't give us the support we need.

8 C: 我和这个分开了一个月都没和家里说。你要说他们就说，“↑啊女生要有点儿自尊心，你这-这都吵架了，这以后还能过吗？”。多少年都不是向着我°。

I was separated from this boyfriend for a month without telling my parents. If I told them, they would say, '↑ Ah, girls need to have self-esteem, you see, you now have quarreled with him, how can you cope with each other in the future?' They have never supported me over the years.

9 T：他们理解不到我们，没法儿理解我们内心的真实的感觉。

They can't understand us, and they can't understand our true feelings deep down.

<table><tr><td>10</td><td>→</td><td>C: 我还挺需要理解和支持的，我如果吵架了，你一个长辈的身份，能帮助到我。我工作不顺利，你帮助到我。你说现在( )((哽咽))多难啊，↑我怎么能就不干了?I need their understanding and support. If I quarrel, you, as an elder, can help me. Should my work isn&#x27;t going well, you can also help me with it. You know how hard the situation is for now( )((choking))↑How can I quit so easily?</td></tr><tr><td>11</td><td>T:</td><td>他们的建议，他们的建议从来不具有建设性啊!Their suggestions, their suggestions are never constructive!</td></tr><tr><td>12</td><td>→</td><td>C: ((哭))((crying))</td></tr><tr><td>13</td><td>T:</td><td>更多的时候是在拆台。More often, they are destroying our plans and making them unsuccessful.</td></tr></table>

In the above extract, C's strong anger towards her parents and strong sadness are displayed. On the one hand, a strong degree of anger is manifested through the following linguistic or non-linguistic resources: (1) prosodic resources. When C complains about her parents, she conveys her anger through a high-pitched register and a tensed voice (Selting 2010: 239). (2) The discursive strategy of recreating the other's speech (Besnier 1990). Specifically, C speaks as her parents and recreates their de-empathic utterances with extra high-pitch peaks (e.g., ‘↑> Don't you have self-esteem? Why are you still with that guy? <’, turn) and in this way displays an angry, aggravated emotional stance. On the other hand, her strong sadness is explicitly demonstrated by vocal cues (i.e., the crying sound and the choking voice in Turn 6 and Turn 10) (Hepburn & Potter 2007). Locating C's emotional reactions in the interactional sequence in which it occurs, they are responding to the discordant rapport which is signalled through C's complaining utterance about her parents.

The nature of the discordant rapport (i.e., ganqing violation-induced) is reflected in the meta-pragmatic comments made by T. Having heard C's complaining way of speaking which displays her parents' de-empathy towards her, T comments C's parents' as not empathic ('They can't understand us', Turn 9). In doing so, T issues a negative assessment of the parents' behaviour, manifesting evaluations of a threat to ganqing, since ganqing emphasizes empathic understanding and emotional understanding (Yang 1994; Chen & Chen 2004: 315). By repeating some part of T's utterance and extending it (Lerner 2004; Vehvilainen 2008), C shows acceptance of T's meta-comment (Turn 10).

Ganqing not only involves one's expectation of being empathically understood and being helped by specific guanxi members but also one's expectation of not being hurt by specific guanxi members.

Extract  $6.5\mathrm{C}$ , a middle school student, complains about her mother.

<table><tr><td>1</td><td>→</td><td>C: 我当时就是把纱窗打开, 想直接跳下去, 我妈一下子把我拽回来, 她说我在威胁她, 然后每次吵架, 我说“我真的是有好几次想去死了”, 她那个态度我真的受不了了。她说“你↑就知道拿死来威胁我们, 你还会干啥?”(哭)) I opened the window and wanted to jump out, and my mother pulled me back, and she said I was threatening her. Every time we quarrelled, I would say ‘I wanted to die’, and I really couldn’t stand her attitude. She said ‘↑ You just threaten us with death, what else would you do?’(crying))</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td colspan="2">T: 她觉得我们是在威胁她? Does she think we’re threatening her?</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td colspan="2">C: 对。 Yes.</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td colspan="2">T: 她说我们威胁她, 大概的意思是你其实并不是想这样做, 你只是想用这样的方式来= She said we are threatening her, which means that you don’t want to do it, you just want to force her in this way to achieve your own purpose =</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td colspan="2">C: =对。她的意思就是, 假如他们不按照我的心愿的话, 我就威胁他们, 我就会从这里跳下去, 但是这一切都是假的, 我根本就不会。 =Yes. What she meant was, that if they didn’t do as I had expected, I would threaten them and I would jump off, but it was all fake, and I wouldn’t do it.</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td colspan="2">T: 当她这么说的时候, 我们的心就更凉了。 When she said so, our hearts were broken even further.</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td colspan="2">C: 对。 Yes.</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td colspan="2">T: ((咂嘴)), 感觉, 就是感觉我们现在的处境, 压力很大哦。也许在父母看来, 他们让我们衣食无忧, 但他们实际上不知道我们有多艰难。 ((Smacking lips)), a feeling, a feeling of where we are right now, we are experiencing a lot of pressure. Maybe in your parents’ eyes, they give us food and clothing, but they don’t actually know how much pain we have psychologically been through.</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td colspan="2">→ C: ……然后很多地方我感觉应该是我对了, 但是她永远觉得是她对。算一道题我算错了, 她算对了, 她就会说“↑你咋这么笨呢!” …In many regards, I feel that I am right, but she always feels that she is right. If I made a mistake on an arithmetic problem and she got it right, she would say ‘↑ Why are you so stupid!’</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td colspan="2">T: ((出声, 声音延长的叹气)) ((A long-voiced sigh))</td></tr><tr><td>11</td><td colspan="2">→ C: 有时候小考我全对, 全班只有几个全对的, 我会特别开心啊, 我去跟她说, 她说“这有啥用? 又不是期中期末!” Sometimes I get all the questions right on a quiz, and only a few students in the class could do that, and I would be very happy. I would tell her, but she replied ‘What is the use of that? It’s not a midterm or a final test!’</td></tr><tr><td>12</td><td colspan="2">T: ((出声, 声音延长的叹气)) 她说话总能那么扎心哦! ((A long-voiced sigh)). She always speaks in such a hurtful way! C: 对…… Yes…</td></tr></table>

This extract revolves around C's prior interaction with her mother. As the details concerning their interaction are disclosed, her anger towards her mother and strong sadness are displayed: (1) by 'quoting and recreating' her mother's criticism of her ('She said  $\uparrow$  you just threatened us with death, what else would you do?', Turn 1) with a high pitch register (Besnier 1990; Reber 2008, 2012). (2) By emotionally sanctioning her mother's inappropriate attitude and displaying annoyance (e.g., 'I really couldn't stand her attitude', Turn 1). As for C's strong sadness, it is observable from her crying sound (Hepburn & Potter 2007). Locating C's anger and anger-related sadness in the interactional sequences in which they occur, these negative emotions are responses to the disharmony between C and her mother (Isik-Güler & Ruhi 2010).

The meta-pragmatic comments made by T upon hearing C's self-disclosure reveal how he understands the nature of the disharmonious relationship that exists between C and her mother. Specifically, T meta/comments C's mother as heart-hurting ('she always speaks in such a hurting way!', Turn 12). In so doing, T makes a negative assessment of C's mother, evoking evaluations of a threat to ganqing. According to prior studies, ganqing involves caring about other's feelings (Wang 2007; Shao & Pan 2019) and not hurting others' feelings (Yen et al. 2017: 109; Zhao & Ran 2019: 269). The discussions reveal that the mother's ignorance of ganqing results in the disharmonious relationship between her and her daughter, triggering C's anger and sadness.

# 6.2.3 Anger and Sadness: Lack of Feelings and Emotional Detachment as Rapport Threat

In addition to feelings, ganqing also emphasizes emotional attachment (Yang 1994; Chang & Holt 1994; Gao & Ting-Toomey 1998; Chang 2013, 2018), inner attachment (Guo 2001), connections (Chen & Chen 2004: 315), or relational connection with others (Hsiang 1974). Though different labels are used, they all point to a common component of ganqing—a close relationship between two guanxi members. Under some circumstances, the unmet ganqing expectations involve two aspects, i.e., lack of feelings and emotional detachment.

Extract 6.6 C's negative emotions are manifested and communicated when she reveals an interaction with an intimate friend Xixi. Their friendship dates to the senior high school period and they are very close to each other for many years. Due to some reasons, C feels estranged from her.

1 C: 我们一起出来，然后你也没有问过我什么，就总是在说你和她们的关系，我是心里有点难过的，而且她还告诉我，她现在有朋友，她们关系很好。

We came out together, you didn't ask me anything but kept talking about your relationships with them. I was a little sad and she also told me she had friends and they were having good relationships.

2 T: 看起来她们更亲密一些。

It looks as if they are more intimate with each other.

<table><tr><td>3</td><td>C: 对。因为这两年我们没怎么联系之后，她总是和那几个朋友一起… …然后我也觉得-她希望就是她的女儿也 大了，去跟那些比较有上进心的啊，优秀的孩子接触…… 她让我也觉得和她离得很远，不太走得近。 That&#x27;s right. Since we have not been in touch frequently these two years, she has been spending time with other friends… And I also think that her daughter has grown up, and she wants her daughter to get in touch with children who are more motivated and aspirational…She gave me this feeling that she was far away, not very close.</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>T: 看起来她好像更在乎那帮朋友，愿意和她们走得更近一些。 It looks as if she cares more about that group of friends, and would like to get closer to them.</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>C: 可能吧! Probably!</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>T: 她也会主动约你吗? Will she ask you out?</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td>C: 就是我们之前的话……((C谈论二者频繁的交往)) Before this… ((C talks about frequent communication between them))</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td>T: 那-那些日子你们还是非常亲密的哦。 You were very close to each other in those days.</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td>C: 可能吧。 Maybe.</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td>T: 后来不知道因为什么原因慢慢疏远了，或者不怎么联系了? So, for what kind of reason, you are dissociated from her or why you don&#x27;t contact her anymore?</td></tr><tr><td>11</td><td>C: 是她还和以前一样，后来会一大早问我啊什么的，我也学她，过很 久才回她，说我有事什么的。在一段时间，她总是在说我，我是 很难过的，好像有一次就是因为一个什么防蚊的一个香囊，就是 她说的我没理解，我再反过来问她的时候，她回的就是“↑你这 都不懂啊，我都已经说得很清楚，这种事情你怎么都不知道？” 让我觉得-好像这个你也太无能了，连这个东西都不知道，或者“ 我的话我怎么说你才能听得懂啊？↑你这个笨蛋！”就这种感觉，这让我觉得我很难过((哽咽的声音))。 She behaved just as before, and she would tell me some of her difficulties in the morning and ask me for advice, but I learned her way and replied to her after a long time by saying that I was busy. She reproached me frequently at that time, which made me so upset. Once I asked her about the anti-mosquito sachet, I didn&#x27;t understand what was told. When I asked her again, she responded by saying ‘↑ You don&#x27;t even understand such a simple thing like this? I have told you in such an explicit way, how can you still know little about this?’ or ‘How else can I make you understand? ↑ You stupid’. This makes me feel very sad ((choking voice)).</td></tr></table>

When C discloses the prior interactions between her and her close friend, her anger and strong sadness are discursively communicated. From the vocal cues (i.e., C speaks with a choking voice and crying sound) and the emotion word ('sad'), C displays strong sadness. As for C's anger towards her close friend, it is manifested in the following ways: (1) complaints about the friend's neglect of her ('we came out together, you didn't ask me anything

but kept talking about your relationships with them', Turn 1). In so doing, C emotionally sanctions the friend's inappropriate behaviour and conveys her annoyance (Langlotz & Locher 2013: 99). (2) By replaying or recreating (Besnier 1990) the close friend's criticism of her in an angry, emotionally aggravated way (Cekaite 2016: 143), as reflected in the high pitch register when C reproduces the friend's speech (' $\uparrow$  you don't even understand such a simple thing like this?', Turn 11). C's negative emotions, which occur when she reports on an interaction with Xixi, are responding to the disharmony that exists between her and Xixi (Spencer-Oatey 2005: 116).

From the meta-pragmatic comments T made on C's self-disclosure, the disharmonious relationship between the client and Xixi can be understood as ganqing violation-induced. On the one hand, he describes Xixi's relationship with the other friends as 'more intimate' (Turn 2), and 'get closer to them' (Turn 4), whereas depicts Xixi's relationship with C as 'dissociated' (Turn 10). In so doing, T means that Xixi has violated the relational principle of ganqing: given that ganqing emphasizes closeness (Wang 2007), connections (Chen & Chen 2004), and emotional attachment (Guo 2001). On the other hand, C's complaining way of speaking indicates that her feelings have been hurt by Xixi ('This makes me feel very sad', Turn 11). Since C complains about how Xixi hurts her feelings, it can be drawn that Xixi has threatened the ganqing with C (Chang 2013; Yen et al. 2017).

The above extract, by focusing on clients' prior interaction with a bosom friend, has illustrated how unmet ganqing expectations pose a threat to rapport and evoke clients' negative emotions. In what follows, more relational dyads between clients and NPTPs are involved, aiming to further elaborate the interrelationship between the GQVI discordant rapport and clients' negative emotions.

Extract 6.7 C's negative emotions emerge when she talks about her relationship with a boy, with whom C has dated for a long time and who has shown good affection towards C.

1 C: 我觉得是不是我自己有问题啊！……我接受不了那样一个落差，就是心里有一种挫败感，就是  $\uparrow$  明明我们关系都这么好了， $\uparrow$  明明都已经是个样子了<，

I am wondering if there is something wrong with me!… I cannot accept such a drop, and there is a sense of frustration, that is,  $\uparrow >$  we are in such good relations. It is already like this<,

2 T:嗯，

Mm,

3 C: 你还说是我误会了，心里面接受不了。我-%我就想是我哪儿不好，是不是长的特别不好看啊，我是不是性格特别不好啊！我内心就接受不了% ((抽泣))……

And you were telling me I misunderstood you, I really cannot accept this. I  $-\%$  am wondering whether I am not good in some aspects, or am I particularly bad-looking. Do I have a particularly bad personality? I really cannot accept her saying that I misunderstood it ((in a sobbing voice)) ...

T: 嗯，Mm,

C：我是在微信上和他认识的。最开始我是不喜欢他的因为他对我很关心，我们挺聊得来嘛。最开始是觉得没有办法接受他的。我是不太满意他的外貌，还有身高什么的，I met him on WeChat. At first I didn't like him, but then I accepted him because he cared about me. We had a lot of topics in common... At first, I felt that I could not accept him. I was not satisfied with his appearance and his stature,

T: 嗯，Mm,

C: ((谈论她在厦门出差时，该男孩具体如何表达关心)) 这个事情就挺让我感动的……后来我发现整件事情的发展好像在我的意料之外。((C talks about how the boy shows concern to her when she has a trip to Xiamen City)). I am deeply moved by what he has done for me… Then I find out that the whole thing seems to turn out beyond my expectations.

T: 这才是-可能是最打击我们的吧！就是[我们] That's - it's probably the thing that hit us the most! [We are

C: [就是我可能-只是想得到他，
[I may just - I just want him,

T: 听你这么说，我感觉，其实你-接受他，跟他在一起，其实是做了-很多的考虑啊=As you talk about him, I feel, you - you accept him, you've considered this a lot=

C: =↑挣扎你知道吗？就是内心 =↑Struggling, you know? My heart struggles

T: 交往那么久，最终决定想他在一起的时候，发现人家根本没想跟我们在一起。就是我们之前做的很多努力其实都是徒劳的。After we had been dating for such a long time, finally, you finally decided to accept him, but only to find that he didn't even want to be with you. That is, plenty of our previous efforts were in vain.

C: 啊，对！……Ah, yes!…

When C discloses a prior social interaction with a boy, her negative emotions manifest. On the one hand, her anger towards the boy is displayed through (1) rhetorical means. That is, the repetition of words ('obviously') and rhythm ( $\uparrow >$  we are in such good relations, it is already like this<sup>+</sup>, Turn 1). (2) Prosodic means. Specifically, the above utterance is produced in a high-pitch register, as well as a fast tempo (Selting 2010: 265). On the other hand, her sadness is communicated through a sobbing voice (Sorjonen & Peräkylä 2012). Understanding these negative emotions in interaction, they are responding to the discordant rapport C has with the boy, as reflected in C's criticism of him.

The disharmony between C and the boy is gangging violation-induced, given the following evidence. One aspect, C's complaining way of speaking ('And you were telling me I misunderstood you', Turn 3) indicates that the boy denies mutual affection between them and his good feelings towards C. Further, the joint construction of T and C (from Turn 10 to 12) indicates

that C has good feelings towards the boy. As it has been previously noted, ganqing emphasizes 'mutual good feelings' (Gao & Ting-Toomey 1998: 24) and 'mutual affection' (Chan 2006). Therefore, C, by complaining about the boy's lack of feelings towards him, occasions an evaluation that the boy's behaviour has violated the relational principle of ganqing. The other aspect, T's meta-pragmatic comment, the content of which describes the boy's desire to detach himself from C ('but only to find that he doesn't even want to be with us', Turn 12), evokes evaluation of emotional detachment as well as the threat to ganqing (Guo 2001; Chen & Chen 2004; Chang 2018).

Extract 6.8 C's sadness is displayed and communicated when she reports on an interaction with her father [C cares about her father and has always expressed her love for him. As for C's relationship with her mother, she does not like her mother because of being mistreated by her mother. C's father has hoped C to do something to ease the tension with her mother but C refuses to do that.]

1 C: 上次咨询结束后((吸鼻子，抽泣))，第二天我给我爸爸打了个电话，我说想找他谈谈，问他有空吗？“他说没空，>↑有什么好谈的？没什么好谈的<”……上周六的时候，我本来就定了自己中午看电影，后来我又买了张电影票，我和他发了信息，%说我邀请你明天和我一起看电影，不管你来不来，你晚上给我回个信息%(（抽泣，哽咽))，然后就没有下文了。第二天我看电影的时候觉得还好，我觉得((哽咽着说))-我不太记得当时什么想法了，我就觉得还好……我觉得我的情绪出来是10月3号还是4号，我上午看到有我爸一个未接电话，我回过去，他没接挂了，过了一段时间他回了个信息，说给我电话是因为要找XX((C的丈夫))，叫他把放在他们那边的盒子拿走，当时XX没接，后来XX回电话了，把盒子拿走了。After the last consultation ((sniffing, sobbing)), I called my father the next day and said that I wanted to talk to him and asked if he was free. He said that he had no time. >↑ What's there to talk about? There was nothing to talk about<’… Last Saturday, I decided to go watch a movie at noon and bought a ticket, % later I bought another one. I sent a message to him and invited him to watch the movie with me the next day, and told him no matter whether he would come or not, he should send me a message by evening % ((sobbing and choking)), but no response from him later. The next day I went to the cinema, it was ok. I felt ((choking))- I don't really remember what I thought at that time, and I wasn't angry or sad. I don't really remember what I thought at the time. I just thought it was okay... Then I felt it was October 3 or 4 when I felt emotional. I found I missed a call from my father, I called back but he hung up. After a while, he sent me a message, he said he was calling me because he was looking for XX ((the name of C's husband)) and asked XX to take away the box that was left in his house. XX didn't answer the call at that time. Later XX called back and took the box away.

2 T: 你说的这些，你是怎么想的？ Do you have any comments about the interaction between you and your father that you have described above?

3 C: 我就是觉得有情绪啊，我会觉得他就是在和一个很普通的人在讲话^就是和你分得很清了，这种感觉。

I feel emotional. I feel he is talking to a very ordinary person, that is, he disassociates himself from me.

4 T: 好像就是刻意用这个话来划清界限了，我给你打电话，不是因为我惦记着你的，是吧？我是有事儿才找你的，让人听了非常心寒。

It seems that he deliberately uses these words to draw a clear line. I am calling you not because I miss you, is it? I called for something, which made us very heartbroken.

5 C: 对，我这周几次都有这种感觉，那种细微的掠过的心寒的感觉，被划了一刀，被刺了一下的感觉。

Yes, I've felt that way a few times this week, a chilling feeling. The feeling of being scratched and stabbed.

In the above extract, C discloses the prior social interactions between her and her father. From the vocal cues—the sniffing, the sobbing, and the choking voice (Hepburn & Potter 2007; Sorjonen & Peräkylä 2012), C's strong sadness is explicitly displayed. Moreover, from the discursive strategy of 'quoting or recreating the other's speech' ( $c > \uparrow$  What's there to talk about? There was nothing to talk about $<$ , Turn 1), C is displaying her negative emotional stance (annoyance) towards her father at the moment (Besnier 1990: 426). By commenting on the father's way of talking with a daughter as emotionless, a similar way of talking with a very ordinary person ('he is talking with a very ordinary person, that is, he disassociates himself from you', Turn 3), C is sanctioning the inappropriateness of her father's behaviour.

C's complaining way of speaking as well as the meta-pragmatic comments made by T reveals the disharmony between C and her father is featured as ganqing violation-induced, which is caused by unmet ganqing expectations. (1) C complains about how she is emotionlessly treated by her father (e.g., the father has rejected her request for a talk and her invitation for a movie, Turn 1; the father talks with C as if C was a very ordinary person rather than his daughter, Turn 3). In so doing, C occasions an evaluation of the father's ignorance of ganqing (Santangelo 2005; Ledeneva 2008; Shao & Pan 2019). (2) T's meta-pragmatic comments point to the father's emotional detachment and distance from C ('it seems that he deliberately uses these words to draw a clear line', Turn 4), and also the father's lack of feelings towards C ('I am calling you not because of I think about you', Turn 4). By mentioning the disconnection and lack of feelings, T occasions evaluations of a threat to ganqing.

# 6.3 Guilt and Anger (and Sadness)

Ganqing not only values social entitlements as discussed above, but also emphasizes 'relational obligation, sacrifice in giving' (Chang 2013: 44), 'living up to one's social obligations' (Yang 1994: 122), and 'mutual obligations' (Hsiang 1974). As far as the content of relational obligation

is concerned, the type of relationship between interlocutors needs to be taken into consideration (e.g., it means filial obligation within child-parent relationships). It is also worth noting that relational obligations, the important components of ganqing, affect people's perceptions of rapport. For instance, Spencer-Oatey (2008: 322) maintains that in collective cultures, 'people's dynamic construal of self can influence various rapport, including the relative emphasis they give to sociality obligation compared to sociality rights'. This means, that if Chinese people perceive themselves as not fulfilling sociality obligations when interacting with others, it would negatively influence their perceptions of rapport, resulting in significant emotional reactions (guilt and anger).

# 6.3.1 Guilt and Anger: Filial Obligation-omission as Rapport Threat

The relational obligation that is emphasized in ganqing, when it is examined in the child-parent relationship, is represented as filial obligations (Gao & Ting-Toomey 1998). Filial piety can be expressed through providing monetary support, it can also be expressed through letting parents live without worry and anguish, to bringing honour to parents through one's academic achievements (Yang 1997; Kwan 2000). Accordingly, if a Chinese self perceives himself/herself as not fulfilling filial obligations, it would result in perceptions of disharmony and the self's negative emotions.

Extract 6.9 C, a man in his early 40s, hasn't received a good education and has changed his job frequently. C's negative emotions are demonstrated and communicated when he recalls a frustrating interaction he had with his mother.

1 C: 这几天，耳边都是我妈妈的声音，“你个败家子，你不节省，家里的钱都让你败光了……”，或者就是“家里拿钱你自己不好好念书，你就是有病，就是恶人，你就应该受到审判，应该受到折磨……”，我心里满满都是内疚感和罪恶感=…These days, my mother's voice is all in my head. ‘You are such a black sheep of the entire family, squandering all the money and not thrifty at all...’ or ‘You take money from home but you don't study hard, you are evil, you deserve to be tried and tortured…’, I am filled with guilt and sin =
2 T: =羞愧。=Ashamed.
3 C: 最受不了就是她对我的谴责，她总说我是败家子啊，钱都让你花了，或者家里不好都是你造成等等，我最受不了就是这个，所有事情都是你承担，所有的不幸或者是家庭的不幸福都是你造成的……，像个罪人，负罪感。

What I can't stand most is her condemnation of me. She keeps complaining that I am the black sheep of the family, that I have spent all the money in the family, or that I am responsible for the bad situation of the family... What I can't stand most is this. I seem like a sinner, and I am guilty.

4 T：可见这份指责-愧疚-的感觉是多么折磨人。

You can see how tormenting this feeling of blame - guilt is.

5 C: 我母亲总是叨叨这事儿，愧疚感，罪恶感很大。

My mother always talks about it, which makes me feel guilty.

C's self-disclosure revolves around the condemnations he receives from his mother. During his self-disclosure, two types of negative emotions are displayed. On the one hand, guilt (a typical type of self-conscious emotion as well as moral emotion) is communicated by using emotion words. On the other hand, through C's complaining way of speaking ('what I can't stand most is her condemnation of me, Turn 3'), the content of which focuses on the mother's criticism toward him, C's anger at his mother is communicated. Locating these negative emotions within the interactional sequences in which they occur, it can be drawn that guilt is triggered by the discordant rapport between the two parties (as indicated by the mutual complaints between them). As for C's anger at his mother, it can be understood as a kind of negative emotion that is triggered by guilt or is located at the later part of the 'emotional interaction chains' (Langlotz & Locher 2017: 310).

Under some circumstances, the complaining context, for instance, the reported speech or reported conversation functions as an assessment (e.g., Drew 1998; Holt 2000; Tannen 2007; Park 2018). By quoting his mother's utterances, whose content revolves around the worries and anguish C has brought to the family (Turn 3), C implicates his failure to fulfil filial obligations. Put in another way, C is occasioning a 'negative assessment' of his person and evoking evaluations of a threat to ganqing. As shown in the analysis, the GQVI discordant rapport threatened by C's unfulfilling of filial obligations has evoked C's negative emotions.

In addition to what has been discussed above, the filial obligation also involves showing care and affection to one's parents, pleasing them, and making them happy (Yue & Ng 1999; Andre 2018). If the Chinese perceive themselves as not doing these when interacting with their parents, it would occasion evaluations of a threat to ganqing and evoke their emotional reactions.

Extract 6.10 C feels guilty when she discloses the interaction with her parents. [C, a girl in her 20s, now serves in the army. Her parents were divorced when she was young. Before this extract, C reports that she asked her father to visit her when she was hospitalized, but this request was rejected by her father for being busy at the worksite.]

1 C: 所以我在他面前，我就只能就靠经济上的，没有钱了

，想花钱，开口找他要。我们的关系就只靠金钱了。

我找他要钱，他又觉得我在他面前只认钱，不关心他。

So, in front of him, I can only rely on his economic support, when I want to spend money, I will ask him for some money.

Our relationship is only based on money. When I ask him for money, he feels that I only care about money, not about him.

<table><tr><td colspan="2">[4 turns omitted]</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>T: 平时这样一些苦闷的话会和谁说说吗? 都是在心里憋着的? 你妈 妈能够理解你? 她即使来陪你, 也很难和她沟通?</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>When you have such difficult moments, who can you talk to? Keeping it all inside yourself? Can your mother understand? Is it hard to talk to her even when she&#x27;s here with you?</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td>C: 我在医院住院的时候, 她也会和我说家里的情况, 他俩 离婚了嘛, 家里的情况都会和我说, 我不想知道这些 情况, 但是我妈就是抱怨。</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>When I was in the hospital, she would also tell me about her family, as she is divorced, I didn&#x27;t want to know about these things, but my mother kept complaining.</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td>T: 她会把你的苦闷扔给你, 会把她的苦闷倾倒给你。 She would pour out her frustration to you, she would pour out her frustration to you.</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td>C: °对°。 °That&#x27;s right °.</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td>T: 但是你本来就很沉重了哦, 越和你说这些你就会感觉到越累。 But you are already in a very difficult situation, the more she tells you this, the more tired you feel.</td></tr><tr><td>11</td><td>C: 当她在我面前哭哭啼啼的, 跟我说那啥的时候, 我心里就会有一 种罪恶感, 我就会有一种自责、负罪感, 就觉得是我们一家人对她亏欠得太多, 作为唯一的女儿, 我做得很少, 就是这种 感觉。</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>When she cries in front of me telling me that, I have a sense of guilt, I have the feeling of self-accusation, guilt, and feeling that our family owes her too much. As her only daughter, I have done so little for her.</td></tr><tr><td>12</td><td>T: 也很无力哦, 想做点儿什么, 好像又做不了什么。只是当她不断 说的时候, 我们能够感受到那种指责, 我们也是有责任的…… We are unable to help however much we would like to-when she keeps talking, we can feel the blame that we are also accountable... for her poor living situation…</td></tr></table>

When C discloses the prior social interaction with her parents, guilt, and anger at her parents are observable. On the one hand, guilt (a typical kind of self-conscious moral emotion) is communicated through the emotion words ('a sense of guilt', Turn 11). On the other hand, from the complaining way of speaking (Turn 1), her anger towards her parents is discernable (Langlotz & Locher 2012). Since C's negative emotions emerge when she talks about the rapport-sensitive issues between her and her parents, they appear as responses to the disharmony that exists between them (Išik-Güler & Ruhi 2010).

The following linguistic cues reveal the causes of the disharmony. In Turn 1, C conveys her father's negative assessment of her through the reported speech ('he feels that I only care about money, but don't care about him'). In Turn 11, C assesses herself as a person who has done little for her mother ('As her only daughter, I have done so little for her'). By quoting or using the negative assessment, the content of which focuses on

C's lack of affection towards her parents (Hwang 1999), and little effort in helping and caring for the parents (Gao & Ting-Toomey 1998: 26), C conveys her failure to fulfil filial obligations (Yue & Ng 1999) and evokes evaluations of threats to ganqing. Summing up, C's ignorance of ganqing causes the disharmonious relationship between her and her parents, evoking her self-conscious moral emotion(guilt). C's anger at her parents can be understood as a secondary emotion that is triggered by guilt (Langlotz & Locher 2017: 310).

# 6.3.2 Guilt and Anger and Sadness: Owing Emotional Debt as Rapport Threat

When it applies to social interaction between friends or long-term collaborative partners, the relational obligations required by ganqing can be realized through acts such as 'responses or returns' (Chang & Holt 1994: 357). Accordingly, if people perceive themselves as not appropriately responding or returning the relational partners' favour (Chang & Holt 1994: 356), it would invoke evaluations of threats to ganqing, resulting in disharmony and significant emotional reactions.

Extract 6.11 C's negative emotions emerge when she self-reports the prior interaction she had with a long-term collaborative partner.

1 C: 就是我以前可能就是想把工作做得越来越好，确实也干得挺好。别的我也不会什么，我也不会关系太乱，但是他这种人，也会指责你，说看我为你做了多少多少多少，你看你男朋友做咨询都是免费的……I might have wanted to do my job in a better way and I made it. I would not do anything else; I don't want to be in a messy relationship, but he would accuse me. 'See, I have done a lot for you. When your boyfriend had counselling here, I even didn't charge you...'

2 T: 那是什么感觉？ How does that feel?

3 C:  $\%$  我不是很好受，我不知道  $\%$  ((哭))。

$\%$  I don't feel well. I don't know  $(\%)$  (crying).

4 T: 那时怎么回应他？

How did you respond to him?

5 C: ((哭))他给我做了，我没有办法，我只能=

((Crying)) He has done it for me, I can't help, I can only=

6 T: =我们欠人家的，

=We owe him,

7 C: 对。

Yes.

8 T: 所以根本不可能-当他对我们不好的时候，我们不可能去怪他。

So, we can't blame him when he treats us badly.

<table><tr><td>9</td><td>→</td><td>C: 就是我就是觉得挺讨厌的。一方面,你明明是为了拉拢我,或让在他那好好干,但是却又说我欠你的,大家就是一个利益共同体,以前我也有这种感觉,就是一个利益共同体,所以我没有太感觉我欠什么,他确实强调这个事儿,I just feel very disgusting. On the one hand, you&#x27;re trying to win me over, or he asks me to work well with him, but on the other hand, you say that&#x27;s what I owe you. We are a community of interests, and I used to feel as such, so I don&#x27;t feel much about what I owe, and he does emphasize it,</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td>T:</td><td>当他强调时什么感觉?What was it like when he was stressing that?</td></tr><tr><td>11</td><td>→</td><td>C: 没有办法,我没有办法再说什么,就是我错了。There&#x27;s no way out, I can&#x27;t say anything more, I&#x27;m the wrong one.</td></tr><tr><td>12</td><td>T:</td><td>是一种很苦闷的感觉,It is the feeling of extreme anguish,</td></tr><tr><td>13</td><td>→</td><td>C: ((哭))((crying))</td></tr><tr><td>14</td><td>T:</td><td>一种打掉了牙往肚子里咽的苦闷。The pain of having to swallow the insult and humiliation silently.</td></tr><tr><td>15</td><td>C:</td><td>对,“我没法儿说-你给我做的这些°()</td></tr><tr><td>16</td><td>T:</td><td>因为我们不占理,Because we don&#x27;t stand on the side of &#x27;li&#x27; (rationality),</td></tr><tr><td>17</td><td>C:</td><td>对,我没法儿( )°</td></tr><tr><td>18</td><td>T:</td><td>No, I can&#x27;t ( )°</td></tr><tr><td>19</td><td>C:</td><td>为什么没法儿说?Why?</td></tr></table>

C's negative emotions arise when she discloses prior interactions with a long-term collaborative partner (collaborative partner for short, and hence after), involving both self-conscious emotion and other-condemning emotion. First, taking responsibility for her wrongful actions ('I'm the wrong one', Turn 11), indexes C's feeling of guilt (Tangney et al. 1996: 1263; Ho et al. 2004: 73). Second, C's anger at the collaborative partner is communicated through the expressive speech act (i.e., the complaint), words with negative connotations ('very disgusting', Turn 9), and the intensifiers (Langlotz & Locher 2012, 2013; Raabis et al. 2019). Third, another guilt-related emotion, strong sadness namely, is explicitly indicated through C's crying sound (Hepburn & Potter 2007; Sorjonen & Peräkylä 2012) and the intensified prosody (Muntigl & Horvath 2014). C's emotional reactions and their situations of occurrence (i.e., C's mentioning of the disharmony between them), reveal that the emotions appear as responses to the disharmony that exists between C and the collaborative partner.

Further analysis of C's complaint and T's meta-pragmatic comments reveals that the disharmony is induced by ganqing violation. First, by

quoting the collaborative partner's utterance, the content of which emphasizes the favours he has done for C (Turn 1), C is conveying a negative assessment of herself—a person who fails to respond to return the emotional debt (Chang & Holt 1994). Second, the meta-pragmatic comments ('we owe him', Turn 6; 'because we don't stand on the side of 'li' (rationality'), Turn 16) also indicate C's failure in responding or returning the favour she has received from the collaborative partner. These analyses reveal that C fails to return the emotional debts and ignores the ganqing that exists between her and the collaborative partner, resulting in the disharmonious relationship between them and her emotional reactions.

# 6.4 Conclusion

This chapter examines the negative emotions that clients display in interpersonal psychotherapy sessions, focusing on the different forms of emotional display and their social-interactional elicitors. Premised on the interpersonal pragmatics approach, the negative emotions accompanying clients' disclosing of the disharmonious relationship between them and the intimate ones are responses to the discordant rapport. The negative emotions and the corresponding social-interactional triggers are the focus of Chapter 6. With regard to emotions, anger, sadness, and guilt are the typical ones. The results indicate that a combination of emotions such as anger and guilt, and anger and sadness, is always observed. Regarding the triggers of emotions, it has been argued earlier in Chapter 3 that ganqing is an essential factor as well as a relational principle that underpins Chinese people's social interaction in intimate and close relationships. Ganqing violation-induced discordant rapport is argued as the trigger of clients' negative emotions. Given that ganqing emphasizes the elements of good feelings, emotional attachment, and reciprocity, and the rapport between clients and people from intimate and close ones can be threatened by a lack of good feelings, emotional detachment, etc., the triggers of clients' negative emotions are further differentiated.

Based on the above foundations, the different types of emotional displays and their elicitors are identified: (1) anger/anger and sadness are emotional displays when clients disclose the unmet ganqing expectation-induced discordant rapport. The rapport threats involve the NPTPs' lack of feelings and emotional detachment when interacting with clients. (2) Guilt and anger (and sadness) are emotional displays when clients disclose the unfulfilled ganqing obligation-induced discordant rapport. As for the rapport threats, they involve clients' filial obligation omission behaviour and clients' owing an emotional debt to the NPTPs.

This chapter also concerns how negative emotions are named and expressed. Few clients name anger explicitly in interaction. Anger is always

Figure 6.1 Types of negative emotions clients display when disclosing ganqing violation-induced discordant rapport.

communicated through the speech act of complaining, words with negative connotations, and prosodically with the high-pitch register. Sadness is more often expressed via vocal cues such as crying and sobbing, and occasionally through emotion words such as 'upset'. Guilt can be named, described, and implicated. For instance, they explicitly name guilt, or describe a wrongful act and take responsibility. Based on the findings presented above, Figure 6.1 is drawn.

# 7 Managing Negative Emotions Through Rapport Management Strategies

# 7.1 Introduction

Based on the theoretical framework—the rapport-orientated management of negative emotions—the chapter explores how therapists manage clients' negative emotions through surrogate-based rapport management strategies. In the previous chapters, it has been discussed that each type of negative emotion has its triggers, i.e., being triggered by the unmet ganqing expectations that exist between clients and the NPTPs or by unfulfilled ganqing obligations, and therefore emotion management is closely related to the types of discordant rapport. In Section 7.2, the analysis focuses on how therapists manage feelings of anger and of anger and sadness that are evoked by unmet ganqing expectations. In Section 7.3, therapists' management of guilt and anger (and sadness) that are triggered by unfulfilled ganqing obligations is discussed.

# 7.2 Managing Anger/anger and Sadness Via Surrogate-based Rapport Management Strategies

Following on from the discussions presented in Section 7.2 concerning the display of negative emotions, I will report how therapists manage these negative emotions. To manage clients' anger/anger and sadness, therapists adopt two different surrogate roles and deploy three types of linguistic strategies, the details of which will be presented as follows. For the following and the other extracts presented in Chapter 7, the turns marked with  $(\longrightarrow)$  indicate the sequences in which the surrogate-based rapport management strategies are involved; the utterances underlined are the focus of the analysis.

# 7.2.1 Surrogating Nptps and Using Accounting Strategies

Accounts are the statements made by social actors 'to explain unanticipated or untoward behaviour'. Having been extensively researched from a remedial perspective, an account is a linguistic device whose function is

to repair norm violations and restore social equilibrium (Goffman 1971: 171-172; Buttny 1993). As far as accounts are concerned, excuses and justifications are the most frequently used ones. The following extract demonstrates how therapists serve as the surrogates for NPTPs (Coupland & Coupland 2001) and account for their behaviour by providing an excuse on behalf of NPTPs, i.e., admitting the action is problematic without accepting any responsibility for it (Firth 1995).

(1) Surrogating NPTPs and appealing to their pressure from third parties

'Duresse by powerful agents' (Schönbach 1980: 197) or higher authority (Semin & Manstead 1983; Antaki 1994) are explanations or accounts people use to minimize their or their co-interlocutors' responsibility for a failure event. During the psychotherapy sessions, therapists surrogate NPTPs and justify their ganqing violation behaviour (i.e., lack of feelings when interacting with clients or emotional detachment from clients) by appealing to pressure from a third party, in this way to tend to clients' unmet ganqing expectations and to manage their negative emotions (i.e., anger/anger and sadness).

Extract 7.1 C feels sad when she self-reports her prior interaction with her father. [C has invited her father to watch a movie and has asked him to give a reply whenever he is available or not, but the father doesn't respond at all. Later, when C notices a missed call from her father, and then she calls back. The call is rejected by her father with a message from him minutes later, informing C that he calls only to ask C's husband to take something away from his home.]

1 T: 未接来电这个事情我觉得很难过……你觉得他真的那么讨厌你吗？I am as upset as you are about the missed call incident that you described earlier… Do you think he really hates you so much?

2 C: 讨不讨厌和我已经没有什么关系了。

It has nothing to do with me whatsoever.

3 T: 还是他做了他自己不得不做的事情？

Or does he do what he has to do?

4 C: 没懂，我没听懂你的意思。

I don't understand. I don't understand what is meant by you.

5 T: 就是说，你觉得他是发自内心里真的不想和你接触，还是觉得自己不得不这样做？比如为了她的老婆远离他的女儿？

In other words, do you think your father doesn't want to contact you deep down, or do you think he has no choice but has to stay away from you, considering that your mother doesn't like you, your father keeps the same attitude as your mother, so he distances his daughter in exchange for pleasing his wife?

C：他不得不做，我相信百分之百，但是前面那条，我也只能相信一半。我觉得之前我很能理解我的爸爸，他现在确实变成了很冷酷无情的爸爸。

He has to stay away from me because of my mother, I believe it  $100\%$ , but on your first point that he doesn't want to contact me deep down. I think I understood my father before, but now he has become a very cold-blooded father.

7 T: 不过我觉得你的一些做法，可能会不会在你爸爸那里头，也会让他很困惑？

I wonder, if we thought from your dad's perspective, would some of your behaviour be confusing from your father's perspective?

8 C: 有什么？

Any examples?

9 T：比如你突然间要找他谈一谈，他会很害怕，这要谈什么啊，他很害怕是不是要作抉择，比如看电影，从来没有这种待遇，或者不知道怎么回复这条短信？

For example, if you suddenly want to talk to him, he will be terrified, wondering what the talk might be about. He might be very afraid of whether you ask him to make a choice, such as watching a movie, for he has never been treated as such, or he does not know how to reply to your message?

10 C:我-

11 T: 他会可能觉得我这把老骨头经受不了这种爱恨情仇的折腾了，想消停一下，好多事情无法面对=

He may feel that 'I am old and don't want to experience completely different attitudes (i.e. sometimes being warmly treated and sometimes being harshly criticised) from others anymore. I just want to have a quiet life and there are so many things that are difficult to settle down' =

12 C: =我这样做是因为我爸爸几个月前在我朋友圈留言……((以正常的语速和语调回忆与父亲愉快的交往经历))

=I do this because my father left a message in my WeChat a few months ago… ((C recalls the happy interaction with her father with normal speed and intonation))

C discloses the prior interaction she had with her father. Using vocal cues (i.e., choking and sniffing in Turn 1), C's deep sadness is manifested and communicated (Planalp 1998). What's more, C's annoyance towards her father is reflected in her complaints about him (Räabis et al. 2019; Selting 2010). Considering the sequential environment of C's negative emotions, it can be drawn that they are responses to the rapport threats she experienced. Specifically, it is the father's lack of feelings towards C and his emotional detachment from her that trigger the ganqing violation-induced discordant rapport (hereafter GQVI discordant rapport) between the two parties and evokes C's anger and strong sadness.

In the response in Turn 1, T begins by showing empathy ('I am as upset as you…'). Thereafter, T acts as a surrogate for C's father to account for his inappropriate behaviour. T's actions can be understood in two ways: (1) T speaks for C's father by describing his beliefs (Mazer et al. 2014: 38). Specifically, T poses alternative questions, with the first alternative question targeting C's prior understanding, thereby suggesting that it is problematic ('do you think he really hates you so much?', Turn 1) and the second alternative question suggesting a preferred understanding ('or does he do what he has to do?' in Turn 3). By presenting such a stance on

behalf of C's father, T aims to account for the father's ganqing violation behaviour; (2) T speaks by using C's father's voice (Tannen 2007) ('… he has no choice but has to stay away from you' in Turn 5). In the first part of her response in Turn 6, C ratifies T's claim that her father must act in a particular way by repeating the main part of it, 'He has to stay away from me because of my mother'. In the final part of her response, however, C continues to complain about her father's emotionless attitude towards her.

As Scott and Lyman (1968) note, in some cases, additional accounts are needed until a remedy is found and ritual equilibrium is restored. Since C is still annoyed with her father and maintains a negative attitude towards him, as portrayed in her speech act of complaint ('he has become a very cold-blooded father', Turn 6), T offers a second account on the father's behalf by appealing to psychological reasons. T speaks using C's father's voice ('I am old and don't want to experience completely different attitudes' in Turn 11). In the following turn, C does not directly ratify T's account but provides reasons for her behaviour (i.e., why she wants to talk to her father and invites him to watch a movie). When C discusses these moments, she speaks in a normal tone of voice and pitch (Couper-Kuhlen 1986: 181; Maynard & Freese 2012: 99) contrasting with her sobbing at the beginning of this extract. A decrease in the intensity of C's negative emotions and the changes in the duration of sadness are evidence of the communicative effect of T's intervention (Schwarz-Friesel 2015; Prior 2016).

To sum up, when confronted with C's sadness resulting from NPTP's ganqing violation behaviour, T acts as a surrogate for the NPTP and provides excuses on his behalf. As for the linguistic realizations of NPTP surrogacy, T addresses the NPTP by using the third-person singular pronoun 'he' and animates his beliefs (when T speaks for the NPTP) or uses the first-person singular pronoun 'I' and animates his thoughts (when T speaks as the NPTP). By acting as a surrogate for the NPTP and providing accounts on the NPTP's behalf, T manages the disharmony between C and the NPTP. From C's responses in the following turns, the surrogate-based rapport management strategy T employs is effective in managing sadness and anger.

# (2) Surrogating Nptps and Appealing to the Misdeeds of Third Parties

As discussed in Chapter 6, ganqing stresses good feelings and attachment, and it is based on these components that people form ganqing expectations. If these expectations are not met, however, it would result in GQVI discordant rapport and trigger interlocutors' negative emotions. The following extract shows how the therapist manages the client's negative emotions by managing the GQVI discordant rapport. More specifically, the therapist offers an excuse on behalf of NTPPs and accounts for their lack of feelings when interacting with the clients.

Extract 7.2 C's annoyance towards her close friends occurs when she reports how she is disrespectfully treated by them. [In the prior part of the extract, C is accused by her close friends of being too vulnerable and irresponsible to her parents.]

1 T: 其实我们得这种病，跟他们对待我们的这种方式也不能说一点儿关系也没有。

In fact, we cannot say that our illness has nothing to do with the way they treat us.

2 C: 但是-每个人不是这么被对待的吗？

But - isn't that how everyone is treated?

3 T：可是他们也有他们的资源啊。也许他们有的资源，我们没有。

But they are also resourceful in their own way. For example, when your close friends are unhappy, they can seek help from their families, who can provide your friends emotional support and assistance. Maybe they have some resources that we don't have.

4 C: 嗯。

Mm.

5 T：他们那样说我们，但并不代表说他们说的就对。

They criticize us in such a way, but that doesn't mean your friends' comments on us are correct.

6 C: 嗯。

Mm.

7 T: 当用那种道德的大帽子拍过来的时候，就是没有人会喜欢你。是吧，告诉你不负责任，你不孝顺，你愧对父母，怎么怎么样，是吧？如果我们这么说他们，他们也不愿意接受。或者-或者-或者再深刻一点说，他们之所以会这样对待我们，也是因为他们曾经被这种方式伤害过。他们只学会了这一种方式，他们不会其他的尊重别人的方式，不是他们坏，是他们不会。

Your friends give you moral evaluations. You are evaluated as irresponsible, not filial. These make you feel ashamed in front of your parents and make others dislike you. They stand on the moral high ground just, won't they? They are claiming et cetera, et cetera aren't they? If we criticize them in such a way, they are not willing to accept it. Or - or - or, to put it more profoundly, they treat us like this because they have been hurt in this way. They have only learned such a way. They will not respect others in other ways. It's not that they are bad, it's because they don't know how to treat people any other way.

8 C：嗯，我也没有怪他们。其实他们也是为了我好。

Mm, I don't blame them either. They do it for my good.

9 T: 最糟糕的就是他们是为了我们好，但是他们做的事情却让我们很痛苦，是吧？=

The worst thing is that when they evaluate you in this way, their underlying intention is good, hoping that you can quickly overcome the difficulties of mental illness. But they achieve their intentions through moral criticism, which is very painful for you. Right? =

10 C: =是，你说的，

= Yes, indeed,

<table><tr><td>11</td><td>T: =对吧?但是我们又不能怼回去,是吧? 因为大家是出于好意。那怎么办呢? =Right? But we cannot retaliate against their moral criticism. Right? Because they criticize us in the hope that we can get out of our psychological distress as soon as possible, and their intention is good. What are we supposed to do?</td></tr><tr><td>12</td><td>C: 都是最亲近的人,最好的人,朋友。 Those who criticize us morally and remind us to quickly get out of the psychological distress are the closest ones, the best people and friends.</td></tr><tr><td>13</td><td>T: 这不是产生抑郁的原因吗?一种打掉了牙让肚子里咽的苦。这种苦越多,人就越抑郁。 Isn&#x27;t that the cause of depression? Just like pulling out one&#x27;s teeth and letting one swallow the pain. The more people suffer, the more depressed they become.</td></tr><tr><td>14</td><td>C: 那,¥也没办法啊,又不能换一拨人¥。 Well, ¥there&#x27;s no way, I can&#x27;t replace my friends with another group of people ¥.</td></tr></table>

In the above interaction, C feels annoyed because her close friends fail to show consideration for her feelings (Fukushima & Haugh 2014) by blaming her as too fragile and not responsible for her parents. Judging from C's complaints towards them, the discordant rapport between them is noticeable and it is the NPTP's ganqing violation behaviour that has evoked her anger. Before T manages the discordant rapport, T provides emotional support by justifying her life circumstance ('we cannot say that our illness has nothing to do with the way they treat us', Turn 1) and conveys to C a sense of being understood (Pawelczyk 2011: 197). In Turn 5, T sides with C and provides emotional support by challenging the correctness of the NPTP's comments ('but that doesn't mean your friends' comments on us are correct'). C minimally responds with a particle  $mm$  that is produced with a slightly falling intonation (Turn 4 and Turn 6), weakly acknowledging T's evaluation (Gardner 1997; Weiste 2016).

Then, T serves as a surrogate of C's close friends and accounts for their behaviour. He addresses C's close friends by using the third-person plural pronoun 'them' and offers an excuse for them ('they treat us like this because they have been hurt in this way', Turn 7). In so doing, T accounts for C's friends' ganqing violation behaviour and denies full responsibility for their actions (Firth 1995: 200). T further speaks for C's friends and excuses their lack of consideration of C's feelings ('It's not that they are bad, it's that they don't know how to treat people any other way...', Turn 7). In her response in Turn 8, C ratifies T's accounts by 'providing further disclosure' (Pawelczyk 2011: 192) and gives a positive evaluation to NPTPs ('They do it for my good'). Thereafter, T provides emotional support by 'speaking from clients' experience' (ibid: 191) and upgrading the emotional aspect of C's experience by verbalizing its emotional load

'…which is very painful for you'). C's ratification of T's emotive expression is observable (as indicated by the interactional strategy of latching in Turn 10).

As for C's response, she replies with a minimal confirming token 'mm' and points out the good aspects of the NPTP's behaviour, which indicates that the excuse is acknowledged by C. According to Firth (1995: 200), 'if the account is honoured, social order is restored' or the 'ritual equilibrium' is restored (Goffman 1971: 171-202). From C's positive evaluation of the NPTPs ('They are the closest ones, the best people and friends', Turn 12), a positive attitude towards their relationship is discerned. What's more, the communicative effect of emotion management is noticeable from the embodiment of positive emotions (Burch & Kasper 2016), which is displayed through her laughter in Turn 14 and later turns (data not shown here).

(3) Surrogating NPTPs and appealing to their impairment

Excuses can be linguistically realized by appealing to NPTPs' physical impairments or the misdeed of third parties (Schönbach 1980; Semin & Manstead 1983). The following is an example:

Extract 7.3 C's anger displays when she discloses how her husband fails to attend to her feelings and needs when she is ill.

[1-4 turns are omitted]

5 C: 我说我胃疼，我老公也不管我。你说原先你总是说我事儿多，我最需要你关心的时候，你不关心我……老公也不关心我……((讲述回到房间后她丈夫的行为)) I said I had a stomach ache, and my husband didn't care. He always complained that I was too busy. When I needed his attention, he didn't care about me…and my husband didn't care about me…((talked about her husband's behaviour after they returned to the hotel room))

6 T: 我的体会哦，也许他一直想关心你，但是他可能在外边，他想保持一点儿尊严。 According to my understanding, maybe he always wants to care about you, but when he is outside, he wants to keep a little dignity. Many men view excessive obedience to women as a lack of dignity. For example, when you mentioned that he was shopping with his leader, even though you suddenly felt unwell and asked him to go back to the hotel to take care of you, he still hoped to continue to be with his leader instead of showing obedience to his wife.

7 C: 那不是啊，我觉得我都有胃病了，他不能这样啊！ That's not true, I think I have stomach trouble, he can't act like this!

8 T: 我刚听你的意思，他私下里头和在人前对你的态度是不一样的。 I just saw what you mean, he treats you differently when there are outsiders than when there are no outsiders.

<table><tr><td>9</td><td>C: 那对啊，就像变了个人似的，太不一样了。
That&#x27;s right, He acted so differently, like a different person. It&#x27;s so different.</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td>T: 其实这方面特别显示出男人的脆弱哦！
This shows the vulnerability of men!</td></tr><tr><td>11</td><td>C: 他脆弱吗？
Is he vulnerable?</td></tr><tr><td>12</td><td>T: 这当然是一种脆弱。他希望自己的老婆在公众场合听他的，给他面子。可能在他的心目中，有的时候男人的面子更为重要。
This is, of course, a vulnerability. He wants his wife to listen to him in public and give him face. Maybe in his mind, sometimes a man&#x27;s face is more important.</td></tr><tr><td>13</td><td>C: 他有的时候就是很好面子。比如他觉得问别人是一种无知的表现，比如问路……
He sometimes cares so much about his face. For example, he thinks asking others is a kind of ignorance, such as asking the way…</td></tr><tr><td>14</td><td>T: 那是一种展现自己无知啊，或者脆弱的一种表现，是吧？
It&#x27;s a kind of showing ignorance or a sign of vulnerability, isn&#x27;t it?</td></tr><tr><td>15</td><td>C: 对。可是他为什么呢，他这样我痛苦啊！
Yes. But why, he makes me so miserable!</td></tr><tr><td>16</td><td>T: 是啊，爱面子是他的一个恶习，如果我们在人前的时候多迎合这一点……
Yes, it&#x27;s a bad habit of him to worry about losing face. If we cater to this point more in front of people…</td></tr><tr><td>17</td><td>C: 我觉得我已经够不和人家攀比了。
I feel like I rarely compare myself with others.</td></tr><tr><td>18</td><td>T: 有没有看那个电视剧-不要和陌生人说话，女主角的老公在外面做得很好，回家就揍她……
Have you watched the TV play named Don&#x27;t Talk to Strangers, the heroine&#x27;s husband behaved very well outside but beat his wife when got home…</td></tr><tr><td>19</td><td>C: 你这么说，我老公这样对我好像还好一些。
If you say so, my husband seems to be treating me better..</td></tr><tr><td>20</td><td>T: 是啊！……
That&#x27;s right!…</td></tr></table>

C's anger is evoked by unmet ganqing expectation-induced discordant rapport. To manage C's anger, T acts as a surrogate for C's husband to account for his ganqing violation behaviour. T's action can be understood as speaking for C's husband by describing his beliefs (Mazer et al. 2014: 18). Specifically, he provides reasons for the husband's inattentive behaviour ('maybe he always wants to care about you, but when he is outside, he wants to keep a little dignity', Turn 6). By presenting such a stance on behalf of C's husband, T accounts for the husband's ganqing violation behaviours.

This account, however, is not ratified by C, as shown in her explicit disagreement in the next turn (Turn 7). Then, T continues to speak on behalf of C's husband by appealing to his impairment (McLaughlin et al. 1983; Schonbach 1980). In attributing C's inappropriate behaviour to his

vulnerability ('This shows the vulnerability of men! Turn 10), T explains why C's husband fails to show concern for C's feelings and needs. T further supports that C's husband has the impairment of vulnerability until this account is accepted by C (Turn 12, Turn 14). In Turn 15, C responds with an acknowledgement token of yes, showing her ratification of T's argument (Pawelczyk 2011; Weiste 2016). C's response also shows the restoration of the social order or ritual equilibrium (Goffman 1971; Firth 1995).

The positive changes in C's emotional status are observable. Before the intervention, C's anger towards her husband is explicitly signalled through the high-pitched voice and the speech act of complaints (Selting 2010; Raabis et al. 2019). C's anger fades away as the intervention continues, which can be observed in the normal pitch when she asserts that her husband is acting in a better way than some of the other men (Turn 19), which compares with her complaining way of speaking when talking about her husband before this extract.

(4) Surrogating NPTPs and appealing to their needs for face maintenance 'The need for facework' (face maintenance or reputation building) is another reason people that people appeal to account for the failure event (Semin & Manstead 1983; Antaki 1994: 31). Therapists surrogate NPTPs and account for their lack of good feelings when interacting with clients.

Extract 7.4 C's sadness arises when she reports that her good feeling towards a boy is not reciprocated by him. [C and an alumnus have known each other for a long time. During this period, the alumnus shows his concern and admiration for C. When C is about to accept the boy as her boyfriend, C is told by him that she has misunderstood him and he doesn't like C at all.]

<table><tr><td>1</td><td>T:看起来学长确实伤害到你了,对吧,是不是?[(已经)It looks like the alumnus did hurt you,didn't he?[(already)</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>C: [↑他伤害到我,是我心里的那种挫败感。[↑He hurt me;it is the kind of frustration deep down.</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>T:觉得好像我们已经-这么熟,我应该觉得[We feel as if we've already - so familiar, I should feel like [</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>C: [↑我觉得你就是在追我啊! =[↑I think you were just chasing me! =</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>T: =对,至少在我感觉他也是在追你的。=Yes, at least I think he was pursuing you.</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>C:我觉得,我都能↑放下我那么多东西和你在一起了,你怎么还那么能说是我误会了呢?I think I can ↑put down so many things to be with you, how can you say that I misunderstand it?</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td>T:也许他是真的喜欢你,但是他可能感觉到你-你只是在眷顾他,是吧?你只是在=Maybe he likes you,but only to feel that you-you were just looking out for him, weren't you? I was really at ease with him, I didn't believe this relationship was fake.</td></tr><tr><td>19</td><td>T: 我也不相信。当你说的时候，我仍然相信他爱你的程度远大于你爱他的程度。Neither do I.
